<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Introduction to Concurrency</h2><a id="user-content-introduction-to-concurrency" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Introduction to Concurrency" href="#introduction-to-concurrency"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Concurrency is when we decompose a program into simultaneously executing tasks.</p>
<p dir="auto">The tasks can:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>run in parallel on multiple cores, OR run multiplexed on a single core</li>
<li>operate on independent data, OR operate on shared mutable data/systems</li>
<li>be launched deterministcally through program flow, OR be lanuched to due external event (button click in UI)</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Concurrency can make our programs more efficient!</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Question:</strong> If a concurrent program only runs on a single core, why would it be any faster than a program that runs serially?
<strong>Answer:</strong> Some tasks involve lots of waiting, not a lot of CPU. During that waiting time, a concurrent program can use the CPU for other useful tasks! For example, downloading multiple photos.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Concurrency With Shared Mutable State</h2><a id="user-content-concurrency-with-shared-mutable-state" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Concurrency With Shared Mutable State" href="#concurrency-with-shared-mutable-state"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Race Conditions</h3><a id="user-content-race-conditions" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Race Conditions" href="#race-conditions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Question:</strong> What will the value of karma be if I run both functions concurrently until completion? Why?</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="int karma = 0;

void do_good_deeds() {
  for (int i=0;i&lt;100000;++i)
    karma++;
}

void be_naughty() {
  for (int i=0;i&lt;100000;++i)
    karma--;
}"><pre><span class="pl-k">int</span> karma = <span class="pl-c1">0</span>;

<span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">do_good_deeds</span>() {
  <span class="pl-k">for</span> (<span class="pl-k">int</span> i=<span class="pl-c1">0</span>;i&lt;<span class="pl-c1">100000</span>;++i)
    karma++;
}

<span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">be_naughty</span>() {
  <span class="pl-k">for</span> (<span class="pl-k">int</span> i=<span class="pl-c1">0</span>;i&lt;<span class="pl-c1">100000</span>;++i)
    karma--;
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong> Answer: Given that each "thread" of execution can be interrupted at any time to run the other, it's impossible to know!</p>
<p dir="auto">The undefined behavior is due to both threads using a <em>shared mutable state</em>; <code>karma</code> is a mutable variable that's shared between multiple threads.
(Race Condition)</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>a key goal of concurrency is <strong>determinism</strong>; code should produce the same result every time, <strong>regardless</strong> of how its tasks are scheduled.</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Safe Concurrency With Shared Mutable State</h3><a id="user-content-safe-concurrency-with-shared-mutable-state" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Safe Concurrency With Shared Mutable State" href="#safe-concurrency-with-shared-mutable-state"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Most modern languages now have built-in language features to make it safer to use shared mutable state.</p>
<p dir="auto">For example, Java's <code>synchronized</code> keyword can be used to limit access to a mutable variable to a single thread at a time.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Models for Concurrency</h2><a id="user-content-models-for-concurrency" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Models for Concurrency" href="#models-for-concurrency"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Two approaches for implementing concurrency:</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Multi-threading model:</strong> a program creates multiple "threads" of execution that run concurrently (potentially in parallel).</p>
<p dir="auto">The programmer explicitly "launches" one or more functions in their own threads, and the OS schedules their execution across available CPU cores.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// Multi-threaded program (pseudocode)
void handle_user_purchase(User u, Item i) {
  if (bill_credit_card(u) == SUCCESS) {
    create_thread(schedule_shipping(u, i));
    create_thread(send_confirm_email(u, i));
  }
}"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Multi-threaded program (pseudocode)</span>
<span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">handle_user_purchase</span>(User u, Item i) {
  <span class="pl-k">if</span> (<span class="pl-c1">bill_credit_card</span>(u) == SUCCESS) {
    <span class="pl-c1">create_thread</span>(<span class="pl-c1">schedule_shipping</span>(u, i));
    <span class="pl-c1">create_thread</span>(<span class="pl-c1">send_confirm_email</span>(u, i));
  }
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Event Driven Model</strong>: a program consists of a queue of functions to run, and an infinite loop (called the event loop) that dequeues and runs each function from the queue, one after the other.</p>
<p dir="auto">When an event occurs (e.g., user clicks a button) the event results in a new function <code>f()</code> being added to the queue which eventually runs and handles the event.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// Event-driven program (pseudocode)
function process_payment() { ... }

setup_event_associations() {
 button = create_new_button(&quot;Pay Now!&quot;);
 button.set_func(ON_CLICK, process_payment);
}"><pre><span class="pl-c">// Event-driven program (pseudocode)</span>
<span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">process_payment</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span> ... <span class="pl-kos">}</span>

<span class="pl-en">setup_event_associations</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos"></span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
 <span class="pl-s1">button</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">create_new_button</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"Pay Now!"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
 <span class="pl-s1">button</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">set_func</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">ON_CLICK</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">process_payment</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Introducing Fork-Join</h3><a id="user-content-introducing-fork-join" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Introducing Fork-Join" href="#introducing-fork-join"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The "fork-join" pattern is basically a concurrent version of divide and conquer:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>first, we "fork" one or more tasks so they execute concurrently...</li>
<li>second, we wait for all those tasks to complete (aka "join") and then proceed.</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">{: .note }
If you're following at home ... this also sounds like a <code>map</code>-<code>fold</code> or <code>map</code>-<code>reduce</code>. Interesting...</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Example:</strong> A parallel sort would be a good example of a problem suitable for fork-join.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="function sort_in_parallel(array, n) {
  t1 = run_background(sort(array[0:n/3]));
  t2 = run_background(sort(array[n/3:n*2/3));
  t3 = run_background(sort(array[n*2/3:n]));

  wait_for_all_tasks_to_finish(t1, t2, t3);
  merge_sorted_subarrays(array);
}"><pre><span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">sort_in_parallel</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">array</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">n</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">t1</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">run_background</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-en">sort</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">array</span><span class="pl-kos">[</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span>:<span class="pl-s1">n</span><span class="pl-c1">/</span><span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-kos">]</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">t2</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">run_background</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-en">sort</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">array</span><span class="pl-kos">[</span><span class="pl-s1">n</span><span class="pl-c1">/</span><span class="pl-c1">3</span>:<span class="pl-s1">n</span><span class="pl-c1">*</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">/</span><span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-kos"></span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">t3</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">run_background</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-en">sort</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">array</span><span class="pl-kos">[</span><span class="pl-s1">n</span><span class="pl-c1">*</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">/</span><span class="pl-c1">3</span>:<span class="pl-s1">n</span><span class="pl-kos">]</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

  <span class="pl-en">wait_for_all_tasks_to_finish</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">t1</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">t2</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">t3</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-en">merge_sorted_subarrays</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">array</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="function task1(param) { ... }
function task2(param) { ... }
function task3(param1, param2) { ... }

function launch_in_parallel() {
  t1 = run_background(task1(42));
  t2 = run_background(task2(&quot;suss&quot;));
  t3 = run_background(task3(3.14, 2.71));

  wait_for_all_tasks_to_finish(t1, t2, t3);
  print(&quot;All tasks completed, proceeding...&quot;);
}"><pre><span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">task1</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">param</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span> ... <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">task2</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">param</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span> ... <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">task3</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">param1</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">param2</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span> ... <span class="pl-kos">}</span>

<span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">launch_in_parallel</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">t1</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">run_background</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-en">task1</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">42</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">t2</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">run_background</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-en">task2</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"suss"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">t3</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">run_background</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-en">task3</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">3.14</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-c1">2.71</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

  <span class="pl-en">wait_for_all_tasks_to_finish</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">t1</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">t2</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">t3</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-en">print</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"All tasks completed, proceeding..."</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Fork-join is often used recursively! For huge datasets, we may choose to split a data source in two (forking). But, if it's still too big, we can split it again! You can imagine this repeating until each chunk is small enough to deal with independently.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Fork-Join In Different Languages</h4><a id="user-content-fork-join-in-different-languages" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Fork-Join In Different Languages" href="#fork-join-in-different-languages"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// C++
#include &lt;thread&gt;

void task1(int n)  { ... }
void task2(int n)  { ... }
void task3(int n)  { ... }

int main() {
  std::cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Forking threads!\n&quot;;
  //To launch a function in the background, we simply create a new thread object.

  std::thread t1(task1, 10);
  std::thread t2(task2, 20);
  std::thread t3(task3, 30);

  // do other processing here...

  t1.join(); //To join, we simple call the thread.join() method. This blocks the caller until the thread finishes.

  t2.join();
  t3.join();
  std::cout &lt;&lt; &quot;All threads joined!\n&quot;;
}"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> C++</span>
#<span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">&lt;</span>thread<span class="pl-pds">&gt;</span></span>

<span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">task1</span>(<span class="pl-k">int</span> n)  { ... }
<span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">task2</span>(<span class="pl-k">int</span> n)  { ... }
<span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">task3</span>(<span class="pl-k">int</span> n)  { ... }

<span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span>() {
  std::cout &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Forking threads!<span class="pl-cce">\n</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>;
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>To launch a function in the background, we simply create a new thread object.</span>

  std::thread <span class="pl-smi">t1</span>(task1, <span class="pl-c1">10</span>);
  std::thread <span class="pl-smi">t2</span>(task2, <span class="pl-c1">20</span>);
  std::thread <span class="pl-smi">t3</span>(task3, <span class="pl-c1">30</span>);

  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> do other processing here...</span>

  t1.<span class="pl-c1">join</span>(); <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>To join, we simple call the thread.join() method. This blocks the caller until the thread finishes.</span>

  t2.<span class="pl-c1">join</span>();
  t3.<span class="pl-c1">join</span>();
  std::cout &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>All threads joined!<span class="pl-cce">\n</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>;
}</pre></div>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-cs notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// C#
using System;
using System.Threading;
using System.Threading.Tasks;

class Program {
  static int task1(int param) { ... }
  static int task2(int param) { ... }
  static int task3(int param) { ... }

  public static void Main(string[] args) {
    int r1 = 0, r2 = 0, r3 = 0;
    Console.WriteLine(&quot;Forking threads!&quot;);
    var t1 = Task.Run(() =&gt; r1 = task1(10));
    var t2 = Task.Run(() =&gt; r2 = task2(20));
    var t3 = Task.Run(() =&gt; r3 = task3(30));
    Task.WaitAll(t1, t2, t3);
    Console.WriteLine(&quot;Joined: {0}, {1}, {2}&quot;,
                      r1, r2, r3);
  }
}"><pre><span class="pl-c">// C#</span>
<span class="pl-k">using</span> System<span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-k">using</span> System<span class="pl-kos">.</span>Threading<span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-k">using</span> System<span class="pl-kos">.</span>Threading<span class="pl-kos">.</span>Tasks<span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-smi">Program</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-k"><span class="pl-k">static</span></span> <span class="pl-smi">int</span> <span class="pl-en">task1</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-smi">int</span> <span class="pl-s1">param</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span> ..<span class="pl-kos">.</span> <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
  <span class="pl-k"><span class="pl-k">static</span></span> <span class="pl-smi">int</span> <span class="pl-en">task2</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-smi">int</span> <span class="pl-s1">param</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span> ..<span class="pl-kos">.</span> <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
  <span class="pl-k"><span class="pl-k">static</span></span> <span class="pl-smi">int</span> <span class="pl-en">task3</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-smi">int</span> <span class="pl-s1">param</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span> ..<span class="pl-kos">.</span> <span class="pl-kos">}</span>

  <span class="pl-k">public</span> <span class="pl-k"><span class="pl-k">static</span></span> <span class="pl-smi">void</span> <span class="pl-en">Main</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-smi">string</span><span class="pl-kos">[</span><span class="pl-kos">]</span> <span class="pl-s1">args</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-smi">int</span> <span class="pl-s1">r1</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">r2</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">r3</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    Console<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">WriteLine</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-s">"</span>Forking threads!<span class="pl-s">"</span></span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    <span class="pl-smi">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">t1</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> Task<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">Run</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s1">r1</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> task1<span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">10</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span></span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    <span class="pl-smi">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">t2</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> Task<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">Run</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s1">r2</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> task2<span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">20</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span></span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    <span class="pl-smi">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">t3</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> Task<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">Run</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s1">r3</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> task3<span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">30</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span></span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    Task<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">WaitAll</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span>t1<span class="pl-kos">,</span> t2<span class="pl-kos">,</span> t3<span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    Console<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">WriteLine</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-s">"</span>Joined: {0}, {1}, {2}<span class="pl-s">"</span></span><span class="pl-kos">,</span>
                      r1<span class="pl-kos">,</span> r2<span class="pl-kos">,</span> r3<span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Python
import threading

def task(n):
  while n &gt; 0:   # do some computation
    n = n - 1

print(&quot;Forking threads!&quot;)

#In Python, we must create a thread object, and then do thread.start() before it runs.

t1 = threading.Thread(target=task, args=(100000000,))
t2 = threading.Thread(target=task, args=(100000000,))
t3 = threading.Thread(target=task, args=(100000000,))
t1.start()
t2.start()
t3.start()

# do other processing here...

t1.join()
t2.join()
t3.join()
print(&quot;All threads joined!&quot;)"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Python</span>
<span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">threading</span>

<span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">task</span>(<span class="pl-s1">n</span>):
  <span class="pl-k">while</span> <span class="pl-s1">n</span> <span class="pl-c1">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>:   <span class="pl-c"># do some computation</span>
    <span class="pl-s1">n</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">n</span> <span class="pl-c1">-</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>

<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">"Forking threads!"</span>)

<span class="pl-c">#In Python, we must create a thread object, and then do thread.start() before it runs.</span>

<span class="pl-s1">t1</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">threading</span>.<span class="pl-v">Thread</span>(<span class="pl-s1">target</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">task</span>, <span class="pl-s1">args</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span>(<span class="pl-c1">100000000</span>,))
<span class="pl-s1">t2</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">threading</span>.<span class="pl-v">Thread</span>(<span class="pl-s1">target</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">task</span>, <span class="pl-s1">args</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span>(<span class="pl-c1">100000000</span>,))
<span class="pl-s1">t3</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">threading</span>.<span class="pl-v">Thread</span>(<span class="pl-s1">target</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">task</span>, <span class="pl-s1">args</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span>(<span class="pl-c1">100000000</span>,))
<span class="pl-s1">t1</span>.<span class="pl-en">start</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">t2</span>.<span class="pl-en">start</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">t3</span>.<span class="pl-en">start</span>()

<span class="pl-c"># do other processing here...</span>

<span class="pl-s1">t1</span>.<span class="pl-en">join</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">t2</span>.<span class="pl-en">join</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">t3</span>.<span class="pl-en">join</span>()
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">"All threads joined!"</span>)</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">"Multi-threading" in Python</h4><a id="user-content-multi-threading-in-python" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: &quot;Multi-threading&quot; in Python" href="#multi-threading-in-python"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Question for the Python program:</strong>
Assuming looping 100 million times takes 5s, how long will this program take to run on a multicore PC?</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer</strong>: 15s
We'd expect all three tasks to run in parallel... taking 5s total. But it takes 15s!
Why? Because when each Python thread runs, it claims exclusive access to Python's memory/objects.</p>
<p dir="auto">So only one thread generally does computation at a time!</p>
<p dir="auto">Why? Python's garbage collection system was never designed to be thread-safe!</p>
<p dir="auto">Python has something called a "Global Interpreter Lock" or GIL.</p>
<p dir="auto">The GIL is like a hot potato  it can only have one owner at a time.</p>
<p dir="auto">Once a thread takes ownership of the GIL it's allowed to read/write to Python objects.</p>
<p dir="auto">After a thread runs for a while, it releases the GIL (tosses the potato) to another thread and gives it ownership.</p>
<p dir="auto">If a thread is waiting for the GIL, it simply falls asleep until it gets its turn.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Question:</strong> So why even support multiple threads? Are there any cases where multithreading speeds things up?</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong> Answer: I/O operations like downloading data from the web or saving a file to disk DON'T need the GIL to run! So these kinds of operations can still make progress if launched in the background!</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">UI Programming and Concurrency</h3><a id="user-content-ui-programming-and-concurrency" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: UI Programming and Concurrency" href="#ui-programming-and-concurrency"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Let's spend a bit of time to see the other approach -- event-driven programming!</p>
<p dir="auto">Event-driven programming is built on <strong>callback functions</strong>. These are functions that are called after an event occurs: after the click of a button, a timer expiring, or a payment completing. Generally, these are used as higher-order functions.</p>
<p dir="auto">Here's a JS-like pseudo-code example:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="function set_up_ui() {
  payment_button = new Button(&quot;Pay now!&quot;);
  payment_button.set_callback(ON_CLICK, call_upon_click);
  add_button_to_ui(payment_button);
}

function call_upon_click() {
  pay_obj = new PaymentProcessor();
  pay_obj.set_callback(call_upon_payment_done);
  pay_obj.initiate_payment_in_background();
}

function call_upon_payment_done(result) {
  if (result == SUCCESS) update_ui(&quot;Payment accepted!&quot;);
                    else update_ui(&quot;Card denied!&quot;);
}"><pre><span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">set_up_ui</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">payment_button</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">Button</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"Pay now!"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">payment_button</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">set_callback</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">ON_CLICK</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">call_upon_click</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-en">add_button_to_ui</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">payment_button</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>

<span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">call_upon_click</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">pay_obj</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">PaymentProcessor</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">pay_obj</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">set_callback</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">call_upon_payment_done</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">pay_obj</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">initiate_payment_in_background</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>

<span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">call_upon_payment_done</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">result</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">result</span> <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-c1">SUCCESS</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-en">update_ui</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"Payment accepted!"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
                    <span class="pl-k">else</span> <span class="pl-en">update_ui</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"Card denied!"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Here, we've added <code>call_upon_click</code> and <code>call_upon_payment_done</code> as callback functions: they are called only once an event occurs. Note that when we pass them to <code>set_callback</code>, we're <em>not</em> calling the functions --- we're passing in the function <em>itself</em> as the argument.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example: Web Browsers in a Slide</h4><a id="user-content-example-web-browsers-in-a-slide" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example: Web Browsers in a Slide" href="#example-web-browsers-in-a-slide"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Consider this overly-simplifed web page.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-text-html-basic notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="&lt;html&gt;
&lt;body&gt;
&lt;h1&gt;Fortune Teller&lt;/h1&gt;
&lt;p id=&quot;fort&quot;&gt;What does the future hold?&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;button onclick=&quot;callbk();&quot;&gt;Get Fortune&lt;/button&gt;

&lt;script&gt;
  set_background_color(BLACK);
  play_mp3(&quot;spooky_music.mp3&quot;);

  function callbk() {
    set_element(&quot;fort&quot;, &quot;You'll ace CS131!&quot;);
  }
&lt;/script&gt;

&lt;/body&gt;
&lt;/html&gt;"><pre><span class="pl-kos">&lt;</span><span class="pl-ent">html</span><span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">&lt;</span><span class="pl-ent">body</span><span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">&lt;</span><span class="pl-ent">h1</span><span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span>Fortune Teller<span class="pl-kos">&lt;/</span><span class="pl-ent">h1</span><span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">&lt;</span><span class="pl-ent">p</span> <span class="pl-c1">id</span>="<span class="pl-s">fort</span>"<span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span>What does the future hold?<span class="pl-kos">&lt;/</span><span class="pl-ent">p</span><span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">&lt;</span><span class="pl-ent">button</span> <span class="pl-c1">onclick</span>="<span class="pl-s">callbk();</span>"<span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span>Get Fortune<span class="pl-kos">&lt;/</span><span class="pl-ent">button</span><span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span>

<span class="pl-kos">&lt;</span><span class="pl-ent">script</span><span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span>
  <span class="pl-en">set_background_color</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">BLACK</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-en">play_mp3</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"spooky_music.mp3"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

  <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">callbk</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-en">set_element</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"fort"</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s">"You'll ace CS131!"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-kos">&lt;/</span><span class="pl-ent">script</span><span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span>

<span class="pl-kos">&lt;/</span><span class="pl-ent">body</span><span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">&lt;/</span><span class="pl-ent">html</span><span class="pl-kos">&gt;</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Here, <code>callbk()</code> is yet again a callback! The <code>onclick</code> property for the <code>&lt;button&gt;</code> element allows you to set a callback. When the button is clicked, it calls that function!</p>
<p dir="auto">But ... how does this work? Overall, browsers work differently than traditional top-down programs. We want the browser to respond to events from the user: clicks, buttons, etc.</p>
<p dir="auto">We can sketch out a Python browser:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class Browser:
  def __init__(self, page):
    self.objs_on_page = self.get_all_objs(page)
    self.run_queue = self.extract_stmts(page)

  def event_loop(self):
    while True:
      self.handle_events()
      self.run_next_statement()

  def handle_events(self):
    for obj in self.objs_on_page:
      if obj.event_occurred():
        func = obj.get_handler()
        self.run_queue.append(func)

  def run_next_statement(self):
    if len(self.run_queue) &gt; 0:
      func = self.dequeue()
      func()"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Browser</span>:
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">page</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">objs_on_page</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_all_objs</span>(<span class="pl-s1">page</span>)
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">run_queue</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-en">extract_stmts</span>(<span class="pl-s1">page</span>)

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">event_loop</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">while</span> <span class="pl-c1">True</span>:
      <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-en">handle_events</span>()
      <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-en">run_next_statement</span>()

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">handle_events</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-s1">obj</span> <span class="pl-c1">in</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">objs_on_page</span>:
      <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">obj</span>.<span class="pl-en">event_occurred</span>():
        <span class="pl-s1">func</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">obj</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_handler</span>()
        <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">run_queue</span>.<span class="pl-en">append</span>(<span class="pl-s1">func</span>)

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">run_next_statement</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-en">len</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">run_queue</span>) <span class="pl-c1">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>:
      <span class="pl-s1">func</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-en">dequeue</span>()
      <span class="pl-en">func</span>()</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The browser keeps track of:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>all objects on the page</li>
<li>a "run queue"</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">The key observation here is the <code>event_loop()</code> function: it's an infinite loop that runs forever! Every time, it:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>checks if the user has done anything (<code>handle_events()</code>); if so, it adds the event to the queue</li>
<li>then, it runs the next statement in the queue!</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Prolog and Logic Programming</h2><a id="user-content-prolog-and-logic-programming" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Prolog and Logic Programming" href="#prolog-and-logic-programming"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Logic programming</strong> is a paradigm where we express programs as a set of facts (relationships which are held to be true), and a set of rules (i.e. if A is true, then B is true).</p>
<p dir="auto">A program/user then issues queries against this these facts and axioms:</p>
<p dir="auto">Logic programming is declarative  programs specify "what" they want to compute, not "how" to do so.</p>
<p dir="auto">Examples:</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Facts:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Martha is Andrea's parent</li>
<li>Andrea is Carey's parent</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Rules:</strong>
If X is the parent of Q, and Q is the parent of Y, then X is the grandparent of Y</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Queries:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Is Martha the grandparent of Carey?</li>
<li>Who is the grandparent of Carey?</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Introduction to Prolog</h3><a id="user-content-introduction-to-prolog" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Introduction to Prolog" href="#introduction-to-prolog"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Prolog is used for theorem-proving (type checking is one such use case; it's in the Java compiler!) and has also been used to implement natural language processing and expert systems.</p>
<p dir="auto">Prolog mostly leans on <em>declarative</em> programming: you specify what you want, but now <em>how</em> you should get there; Prolog is responsible for figuring that out!</p>
<p dir="auto">When given a query, Prolog tries to find a chain of connections between the query and the specified facts and rules that lead to an answer.</p>
<p dir="auto">Every Prolog program is comprised of facts about the world, and a bunch of rules that can be used to discover new facts.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Prolog Facts</h3><a id="user-content-prolog-facts" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Prolog Facts" href="#prolog-facts"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">A "fact" is a predicate expression that declares either...</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>An attribute about some thing (aka an atom); you can think of this as being "always true"
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>outgoing(ren)</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>A relationship between two or more atoms or numbers:
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>parent(alice, bob)</code></li>
<li><code>age(ren, 80)</code></li>
<li><code>teaches(carey, course(cs, 131))</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Implicitly, we're defining some terms:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>an "atom" is a "thing". In the above examples, this includes <code>ren</code>, <code>alice</code>, and <code>bob</code>. They <strong>must be lowercase</strong>.</li>
<li>a "functor" is like a function (or relationship). In the above examples, this includes <code>outgoing</code>, <code>parent</code>, and <code>age</code>. They <strong>must be lowercase</strong>.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">If a fact isn't explicitly stated, it is false. For example, in the above case, since we didn't explicitly state it, <code>alice</code> is not outgoing.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Prolog Rules</h3><a id="user-content-prolog-rules" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Prolog Rules" href="#prolog-rules"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">A rule lets us define a new fact in terms of one or more existing facts or rules.</p>
<p dir="auto">Each rule has two parts...</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>A "head" which defines what the rule is trying to determine</li>
<li>A "body" which specifies the conditions (aka subgoals) that allow us to conclude the head is true</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Rules can be defined with atoms, numbers, or <em>variables</em>. Variables like <code>X</code> and <code>Y</code> are like placeholders which Prolog will try to fill in as it tries to answer user queries. <strong>Variables must always be capitalized</strong>.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-prolog notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="% Facts:
outgoing(ren).
silly(ren).
parent(alice, bob).
age(ren, 80).
parent(bob, carol).

% Rules:
comedian(P) :- silly(P), outgoing(P).
grandparent(X, Y) :- parent(X,Q), parent(Q,Y).
old_comedian(C) :- comedian(C),
age(C, A), A &gt; 60."><pre><span class="pl-c">% Facts:</span>
<span class="pl-en">outgoing</span>(<span class="pl-c1">ren</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>
<span class="pl-en">silly</span>(<span class="pl-c1">ren</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>
<span class="pl-en">parent</span>(<span class="pl-c1">alice</span>, <span class="pl-c1">bob</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>
<span class="pl-en">age</span>(<span class="pl-c1">ren</span>, <span class="pl-c1">80</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>
<span class="pl-en">parent</span>(<span class="pl-c1">bob</span>, <span class="pl-c1">carol</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>

<span class="pl-c">% Rules:</span>
<span class="pl-en">comedian</span>(<span class="pl-v">P</span>) <span class="pl-k">:-</span> silly(<span class="pl-v">P</span>), outgoing(<span class="pl-v">P</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>
<span class="pl-en">grandparent</span>(<span class="pl-v">X</span>, <span class="pl-v">Y</span>) <span class="pl-k">:-</span> parent(<span class="pl-v">X</span>,<span class="pl-v">Q</span>), parent(<span class="pl-v">Q</span>,<span class="pl-v">Y</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>
<span class="pl-en">old_comedian</span>(<span class="pl-v">C</span>) <span class="pl-k">:-</span> comedian(<span class="pl-v">C</span>),
age(<span class="pl-v">C</span>, <span class="pl-v">A</span>), <span class="pl-v">A</span> <span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">60</span><span class="pl-k">.</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">{: .note }</p>
<p dir="auto">Rules and facts might seem very different, but I (Matt) argue that they aren't! You could think of a fact as a rule that has no body. Then, it is <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vacuous_truth" rel="nofollow">vacuously true</a> (and thus, always true).</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Recursive Rules</h4><a id="user-content-recursive-rules" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Recursive Rules" href="#recursive-rules"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Rules can also be recursive and can have multiple parts!</p>
<p dir="auto">Similar to recursion and pattern matching in Haskell, Prolog processes rules from the top to the bottom. So, the base case(s) should always go first!</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-prolog notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="% Recursive rules:
ancestor(X, Z) :- parent(X,Z).
ancestor(X, Z) :- parent(X,Y), ancestor(Y,Z)."><pre><span class="pl-c">% Recursive rules:</span>
<span class="pl-en">ancestor</span>(<span class="pl-v">X</span>, <span class="pl-v">Z</span>) <span class="pl-k">:-</span> parent(<span class="pl-v">X</span>,<span class="pl-v">Z</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>
<span class="pl-en">ancestor</span>(<span class="pl-v">X</span>, <span class="pl-v">Z</span>) <span class="pl-k">:-</span> parent(<span class="pl-v">X</span>,<span class="pl-v">Y</span>), ancestor(<span class="pl-v">Y</span>,<span class="pl-v">Z</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Explanation of the above code block:</p>
<p dir="auto">X is the ancestor of Z if:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>X is Z's parent</li>
<li>OR if X is some person Y's parent AND Y is an ancestor of person Z</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">{: .note }
Prolog uses something called the "closed-world assumption" (CWA). Basically, this means that only things that can be proven true by the program are true; <em>everything else</em> is false.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Negation in Rules</h4><a id="user-content-negation-in-rules" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Negation in Rules" href="#negation-in-rules"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Rules can also use negation  but be careful!</p>
<p dir="auto">In Prolog, <code>not(something)</code> works as follows:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>Prolog tries to prove <code>something</code> is true using all of the program's facts and rules</li>
<li>If <code>something</code> can't be proven as true, then <code>not(something)</code> is found to be true.</li>
</ol>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-prolog notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="% Rules with negation:
serious(X) :- not(silly(X))."><pre><span class="pl-c">% Rules with negation:</span>
<span class="pl-en">serious</span>(<span class="pl-v">X</span>) <span class="pl-k">:-</span> not(silly(<span class="pl-v">X</span>))<span class="pl-k">.</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">For example, the query <code>serious(alice)</code> is true, since the closed-world assumption says that <code>silly(alice)</code> is false.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Prolog Queries</h2><a id="user-content-prolog-queries" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Prolog Queries" href="#prolog-queries"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">We can create queries to answer true/false questions:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>A query can match a simple fact...</li>
<li>Or it can execute a rule.</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-prolog notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="?- outgoing(alice)
true
?- grandparent(brenda, ned)
true"><pre>?- outgoing(alice)
<span class="pl-en">true</span>
?- grandparent(<span class="pl-c1">brenda</span>, <span class="pl-c1">ned</span>)
<span class="pl-c1">true</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">We can also create queries to fill-in-the-blanks:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>The query will find ALL possible matches.</li>
<li>The query can specify multiple unknowns.</li>
<li>And Prolog will find ALL consistent combinations of answers!</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="?- parent(alice , Who)
Who = bob
Who = brenda
?- grandparent(A, B)

%answers to queries below
A = alice, B = caitlin
A = brenda, B = ned"><pre class="notranslate"><code>?- parent(alice , Who)
Who = bob
Who = brenda
?- grandparent(A, B)

%answers to queries below
A = alice, B = caitlin
A = brenda, B = ned
</code></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Resolution: How Prolog Answers Queries</h2><a id="user-content-resolution-how-prolog-answers-queries" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Resolution: How Prolog Answers Queries" href="#resolution-how-prolog-answers-queries"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Example facts/rules:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-prolog notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="parent (nel, ted).
parent (ann, bob).
parent (ann, bri).
parent (bri, cas).
gparent( X ,  Y )  :-
  parent(X,Q), parent(Q,Y)."><pre><span class="pl-en">parent</span> (<span class="pl-c1">nel</span>, <span class="pl-c1">ted</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>
<span class="pl-en">parent</span> (<span class="pl-c1">ann</span>, <span class="pl-c1">bob</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>
<span class="pl-en">parent</span> (<span class="pl-c1">ann</span>, <span class="pl-c1">bri</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>
<span class="pl-en">parent</span> (<span class="pl-c1">bri</span>, <span class="pl-c1">cas</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span>
<span class="pl-en">gparent</span>( <span class="pl-v">X</span> ,  <span class="pl-v">Y</span> )  <span class="pl-k">:-</span>
  parent(<span class="pl-v">X</span>,<span class="pl-v">Q</span>), parent(<span class="pl-v">Q</span>,<span class="pl-v">Y</span>)<span class="pl-k">.</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Example query:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-prolog notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="gparent(ann, W)"><pre><span class="pl-en">gparent</span>(<span class="pl-c1">ann</span>, <span class="pl-v">W</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Algorithm:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>Add our query to a goal stack</li>
<li>Pop the top goal in our goal stack and match it with each item in our database, from top to bottom</li>
<li>If we find a match, extract the variable mappings, and create a new map with the old+new mappings</li>
<li>Create a new goal stack, copying over existing, unprocessed goals and adding new subgoals</li>
<li>Recursively repeat the process on the new goal stack and the new mappings</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">So initially, our goal stack is simply <code>gparent(ann,W)</code>, and our mappings are <code>{}</code>.
Then, after matching the last rule, our goal stack becomes:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="parent(X,Q)
parent(Q,Y)"><pre class="notranslate"><code>parent(X,Q)
parent(Q,Y)
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">And our mappings are <code>{X-&gt;ann,W&lt;-&gt;Y}</code></p>
<p dir="auto">Then, pop the top rule off our goal stack. We have a potential match with <code>parent (nel, ted)</code>. So our goal stack becomes:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="parent(Q,Y)"><pre class="notranslate"><code>parent(Q,Y)
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">With the mappings: <code>{X-&gt;ann,W&lt;-&gt;Y, Q-&gt;bob}</code></p>
<p dir="auto">We pop the top rule off the stack again. There's no rule that matches <code>parent(bob,Y)</code>, which means the set of mappings we discovered were not valid.</p>
<p dir="auto">So we'll back-track one level up and continue searching for alternative mappings.</p>
<p dir="auto">If our goal stack is empty, we output variables from our mapping that were explicitly queried; in this case, our final mapping is:
<code>{ X -&gt;ann, W &lt;-&gt; Y &lt;-&gt; cas, Q -&gt;bri }</code></p>
<p dir="auto">So we return <code>cas</code>, since <code>W=cas</code>.</p>
</article></div><button hidden=""></button></section></div></div></div> <!-- --> <!-- --> </div></div></div><div class="Box-sc-g0xbh4-0"></div></div></div></div></div><div id="find-result-marks-container" class="Box-sc-g0xbh4-0 cCoXib"></div><button hidden="" data-testid="" data-hotkey-scope="read-only-cursor-text-area"></button><button hidden=""></button></div> <!-- --> <!-- --> <script type="application/json" id="__PRIMER_DATA_:R0:__">{"resolvedServerColorMode":"day"}</script></div>
</react-app>
</turbo-frame>



  </div>

</turbo-frame>

    </main>
  </div>

  </div>
